<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7539393555438967539">"Dad says we are going to grow vegetable soup." So begins Lois Ehlert’s bright, bold picture book about vegetable gardening for the very young. The necessary tools are pictured and labeled, as are the seeds (green bean, pea, corn, zucchini squash, and carrot). Then the real gardening happens . . . planting, weeding, harvesting, washing, chopping, and cooking! In the end? "</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7539393555438967539">"Dad says we are going to grow vegetable soup." So begins Lois Ehlert’s bright, bold picture book about vegetable gardening for the very young. The necessary tools are pictured and labeled, as are the seeds (green bean, pea, corn, zucchini squash, and carrot). Then the real gardening happens . . . planting, weeding, harvesting, washing, chopping, and cooking! In the end? "It was the best soup ever." Ehlert’s simple, colorful cut-paper-style illustrations are child-friendly, as is the big black type. A recipe for vegetable soup tops it all off!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7539393555438967539">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer650411300">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8139672709666168768">This is a book that I enjoy reading every Spring with my children. You an talk about vegetables and fruits and their differences, you can cook vegetable soup in your classroom and share it as snack. You can do a picture walk first, then have a copy of the book in the different centers and plan different activities such as:<br />Sensory center: bring the actual vegetables and have them in a center where the children will explore the different smells and will touch different textures in fruits and veget</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8139672709666168768">This is a book that I enjoy reading every Spring with my children. You an talk about vegetables and fruits and their differences, you can cook vegetable soup in your classroom and share it as snack. You can do a picture walk first, then have a copy of the book in the different centers and plan different activities such as:<br />Sensory center: bring the actual vegetables and have them in a center where the children will explore the different smells and will touch different textures in fruits and vegetables.<br />Math Center: Children will create a venn diagram and will classify fruits and vegetables based in their differences and similitudes. <br />Cook Center: Cook with your students vegetable soup as a Friday activity<br />Literacy Center: Retelling the story. Bring props and ask the students to recreate the story.<br />It is a wonderful book!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1717864.Growing_Vegetable_Soup" title="Hardcover 9780152325756" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18426425-meghan-brennan?shelf=literacy" class="actionLinkLite">literacy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1444426470">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15244730563975830691">In this colorful book, a father and son plant vegetables to make a vegetable soup. They plant seeds, watch the seeds sprout, and grow into plants. When the vegetables are ready to be picked, they dig them up and bring them home. At home, they wash them, cut them up, and make a delicious vegetable soup. This books bright illustrations and simple language make it perfect for a toddler classroom, but could be used in older classrooms during an activity to introduce planting and harvesting or cookin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15244730563975830691">In this colorful book, a father and son plant vegetables to make a vegetable soup. They plant seeds, watch the seeds sprout, and grow into plants. When the vegetables are ready to be picked, they dig them up and bring them home. At home, they wash them, cut them up, and make a delicious vegetable soup. This books bright illustrations and simple language make it perfect for a toddler classroom, but could be used in older classrooms during an activity to introduce planting and harvesting or cooking and following a recipe. This book could be used to teach vocabulary with a picture matching activity since each vegetable and tool is labeled in the book. This book could be on the shelf during a farm unit, gardening unit, or food unit.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6541276048093557218">Growing Vegetable Soup by <a title="Lois Ehlert" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10950.Lois_Ehlert">Lois Ehlert</a> explains the process of growing vegetables, starting from seeds all the way to making a pot of soup. A child gathers tools, plants seeds and sprouts, then watches their growth. When the vegetables are ripe, they get picked and pulled, then cut up and cooked into soup. A recipe is included to make vegetable soup at the end of the book.<br /><br />As someone who grew up on a farm with a huge garden, I love that this book introduces the experience of vegetable gardening to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6541276048093557218">Growing Vegetable Soup by <a title="Lois Ehlert" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10950.Lois_Ehlert">Lois Ehlert</a> explains the process of growing vegetables, starting from seeds all the way to making a pot of soup. A child gathers tools, plants seeds and sprouts, then watches their growth. When the vegetables are ripe, they get picked and pulled, then cut up and cooked into soup. A recipe is included to make vegetable soup at the end of the book.<br /><br />As someone who grew up on a farm with a huge garden, I love that this book introduces the experience of vegetable gardening to many children. Eating food that you have grown is a fulfilling experience. <br /><br />The text features a large bold font telling the gardening story, while all the pictured items, including tools, seeds, plants, kitchen utensils and soupware are labeled in smaller type. Gardening and cooking vocabulary is used both in the text and labeled items.<br /><br />The clear, bright colors should appeal to young readers. Some may feel the colors shown are too bright and almost garish at times.<br /><br />There are many ways to extend the story, including language, cooking,<br />art, writing and vocabulary. <br /><br />For ages 3 to 6, read-aloud, gardening, vegetables, seeds, cooking, season themes and fans of Lois Ehlert.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8795365878290512966">Characters: Dad and child <br />Point of View: First Person from the child <br />Setting: Garden <br />Lexile level: 140 L Primary Grades <br />Genre: Picture Book<br /><br /><br />Plot:In the beginning, a child mentions, "Dad says we are going to grow vegetable soup." <span id="freeTextContainer9992186238817785292">it's one of my favorites. not just because for nostalgia reasons, but even before, as a five year old, i remember i really liked, and still do, the colors and the art work presented in the book. it's like cut-outs of paper, yet it's true to the real thing. i liked how the tools and vegetables on the page have labels, aside from the large text of the actual story. i mean the illustrator/author even labels the "worm" found in the broccoli. how's that for organically grown food. no pesticides. ther</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9992186238817785292">it's one of my favorites. not just because for nostalgia reasons, but even before, as a five year old, i remember i really liked, and still do, the colors and the art work presented in the book. it's like cut-outs of paper, yet it's true to the real thing. i liked how the tools and vegetables on the page have labels, aside from the large text of the actual story. i mean the illustrator/author even labels the "worm" found in the broccoli. how's that for organically grown food. no pesticides. there are no outlines on the illustrations which was one of the reasons, why i think the book art was all comprised of cut-outs, but none the less they are very detailed yet simple.<br /><br />i don't know how my parents thought of the book, but speaking from my point of view as a person who has had the book since childhood, it's a good book. i would recommend this book, but only for children who are creative. Children who like video games and watch nickelodeon or disney would not be a good candidate. why? because they probably wont be impressed by simplicity and static artwork. though i must admit, when i was a child i watched my fair share of tv shows such as lamb chop's play-along, reading rainbow, sesame street, and some 3-2-1 contact.<br /><br />i've had this book since i was in kindergarten back in the early 90s. i still have it on my book shelf, though it has seen better days. the cover is now faded and the binding held together by tape. I was five when i first read this book. I remember ordering this through those book orders schools would get and distribute in class for interested students. </span>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer92796773">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5769437956498841516">In another wonderful fall themed book, Lois Ehlert uses a simple story and wonderful pictures to show the reader how to group vegetable soup. The story begins with the idea of growing soup, an idea foreign to children that do not live in an area where is is easy such as I did out West. The child gathers tools and plants the seeds and then watches them grow in the warm sun. Once the vegetables are ready, they are picked and pulled and cut up for soup. The story ends with the anticipation of doing</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5769437956498841516">In another wonderful fall themed book, Lois Ehlert uses a simple story and wonderful pictures to show the reader how to group vegetable soup. The story begins with the idea of growing soup, an idea foreign to children that do not live in an area where is is easy such as I did out West. The child gathers tools and plants the seeds and then watches them grow in the warm sun. Once the vegetables are ready, they are picked and pulled and cut up for soup. The story ends with the anticipation of doing it again next year. There is even a recipe at the end of the book for the reader to make their own vegetable soup.<br />Possible uses: Vermont seasons, nature, fresh foods, cooking.<br />I think this would be a fun book to read to students. Students could sign up to bring in different vegetables (grown in their own gardents if possible) and make their own soup. Children are notoriously picky eaters, but when they have a hand in preparation it is amazing what they will try.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5577316026572941466">I actually read a Red Wagon 2004 very large board book edition of this book. <br /><br />I love the idea of this: watching the evolution of planting seeds for vegetables to picking or digging out the vegetables, and making the soup with them, and a recipe is even included in the back of the book.<br /><br />I always loved all but a very few vegetables but I could see parents and other adults using this book (along with the activities it depicts) with toddlers and preschoolers to encourage them to eat vegetables.<br /><br />I alway</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5577316026572941466">I actually read a Red Wagon 2004 very large board book edition of this book. <br /><br />I love the idea of this: watching the evolution of planting seeds for vegetables to picking or digging out the vegetables, and making the soup with them, and a recipe is even included in the back of the book.<br /><br />I always loved all but a very few vegetables but I could see parents and other adults using this book (along with the activities it depicts) with toddlers and preschoolers to encourage them to eat vegetables.<br /><br />I always wanted a vegetable garden when I was a kid. For those children who can participate in growing and picking/digging vegetables, then cooking them into a soup, this is a good introductory book.<br /><br />I found the colors used in the illustrations garish and not particularly appealing; the vegetables were simply too bright for me. Kids may like the vivid colors though. The idea of the vegetables and the soup (it’s a cold day) was enticing.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5577316026572941466">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/650330776?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 15, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21218746-lanyisha" class="user" title="Lanyisha">Lanyisha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer650330776">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12947685724144962061">This book told a story about a family that was growing a garden to pick the vegetables to make vegetable soup. The author used foreshadowing in the book. It showed the characters in the book planting seeds. It showed the vegetables growing. It showed the characters picking the vegetables and chopping them up. As I read the book my students would guess what was going to happen next. This is why I think the author did a good job in using foreshadowing. If the book was not named Growing Vegetable S</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12947685724144962061">This book told a story about a family that was growing a garden to pick the vegetables to make vegetable soup. The author used foreshadowing in the book. It showed the characters in the book planting seeds. It showed the vegetables growing. It showed the characters picking the vegetables and chopping them up. As I read the book my students would guess what was going to happen next. This is why I think the author did a good job in using foreshadowing. If the book was not named Growing Vegetable Soup I think that my students would still have been able to predict that the vegetables were going to be used to make a vegetable soup. I would teach the techniques of foreshadowing by sharing with my students that you can use foreshadowing in all types of stories. I usually see it used in a mystery or suspense story, but it can be used to tell a story as simple as the one in this book. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12947685724144962061">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/310173396?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1533441-shanna-gonzalez" class="user" title="Shanna Gonzalez">Shanna Gonzalez</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1533441-shanna-gonzalez?shelf=children-00-04" class="actionLinkLite">children-00-04</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer310173396">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11113163436737516375">This simple story introduces children to the basic growing cycle of garden vegetables. It opens with a child narrator stating, "Dad says we're going to grow vegetable soup." The narrator then explains in simple terms how the family goes about cultivating their vegetables, from planting to harvest. Ehlert illustrates each step with her characteristic collage-style art, more abstract than some of her other work. This is a great introduction to the joy of gardening, and the fact that this garden is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11113163436737516375">This simple story introduces children to the basic growing cycle of garden vegetables. It opens with a child narrator stating, "Dad says we're going to grow vegetable soup." The narrator then explains in simple terms how the family goes about cultivating their vegetables, from planting to harvest. Ehlert illustrates each step with her characteristic collage-style art, more abstract than some of her other work. This is a great introduction to the joy of gardening, and the fact that this garden is a family project, culminating in a shared meal of soup, imbues the story with relational warmth.<br /><br />With its predictable, simple text and visual warmth, this is a great preschooler read-aloud. It may also be enjoyed by early readers, although they might need help reading the names of vegetables.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7621239155388752097">Lois Ehlert grew up in Wisconsin into a family that was always making and creating. Her mother was a seamstress and her father had a fully stocked workshop in his basement containg tools, lumber and art supplies. Lois Ehlerts art style is collage. She creates her art by cutting each paper piece one at a time. Her favorite subjects are nature and animals. I picked the book growing vegetable soup due to its simple introduction to vegetable vocabulary. I like to use this book when we are discussing spring and planting. I have a clear root vegetable growung kit. The children choose the root vegetables and we observe and document the growth in our journals.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer308308262">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer190685800633322020">Many of my students do not know where their food originates. This book helps kids make the connection between the garden and the table. In the story the father announces to his family that they are going to "grow vegetable soup." The author then describes how the family raises a vegetable garden to make "the best soup ever." A recipe for the tasty soup is also included in the book. Some of my student begged me to make a copy of it to take home. I don't know how many families will actually make i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText190685800633322020">Many of my students do not know where their food originates. This book helps kids make the connection between the garden and the table. In the story the father announces to his family that they are going to "grow vegetable soup." The author then describes how the family raises a vegetable garden to make "the best soup ever." A recipe for the tasty soup is also included in the book. Some of my student begged me to make a copy of it to take home. I don't know how many families will actually make it but, as a teacher, it was fun to hear young children wanting to try "vegetable" soup.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer426992993">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4293334130012849497">Growing vegetable soup is an adorable book about growing all of the vegetables one would need to make a delicious vegetable stew. Each page talks about the growing process and has big bold pictures so young children can follow along. The tools required to grow vegetables are all in this book, so students who grew up in town can learn about something that they otherwise would never have been exposed to. It is also labeled which is nice so children can pick the book up on their own and instead of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4293334130012849497">Growing vegetable soup is an adorable book about growing all of the vegetables one would need to make a delicious vegetable stew. Each page talks about the growing process and has big bold pictures so young children can follow along. The tools required to grow vegetables are all in this book, so students who grew up in town can learn about something that they otherwise would never have been exposed to. It is also labeled which is nice so children can pick the book up on their own and instead of reading the story, can simply walk through the book and look at what the different pictures are.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer696269360">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4113065088210888517">"Growing Vegetable Soup" is a wonderful addition to our summer gardening books. Ehlert created simple illustrations to follow along in the steps of gardening. One of my favourite things that sets Ehlert's books apart is the labeling and teaching of the seeds, tools and all the items used for gardening and making soup. I enjoy seeing the various plants grow on several pages and love the recipe at the end of the story. The pages on this book carry with them the joy experienced through out the plan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4113065088210888517">"Growing Vegetable Soup" is a wonderful addition to our summer gardening books. Ehlert created simple illustrations to follow along in the steps of gardening. One of my favourite things that sets Ehlert's books apart is the labeling and teaching of the seeds, tools and all the items used for gardening and making soup. I enjoy seeing the various plants grow on several pages and love the recipe at the end of the story. The pages on this book carry with them the joy experienced through out the planting and growing season, a joy which is crucial to impart to our children.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9450564260228702393">I like this book a lot because it shows a family growing several vegetables needed to make vegetable soup. It even has a recipe for vegetable soup in the back. I think this would be great of a plant lesson. If possible it wold be really awesome to have the class split up into groups and each grow a vegetable. Then, whether the plants grew well or not the class could get the ingredients and make vegetable soup to try. <br />Grade: 2nd- life cycle of plants, 5th- an object is the sum of its parts: find</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9450564260228702393">I like this book a lot because it shows a family growing several vegetables needed to make vegetable soup. It even has a recipe for vegetable soup in the back. I think this would be great of a plant lesson. If possible it wold be really awesome to have the class split up into groups and each grow a vegetable. Then, whether the plants grew well or not the class could get the ingredients and make vegetable soup to try. <br />Grade: 2nd- life cycle of plants, 5th- an object is the sum of its parts: find the mass before and after combining to make the soups. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  }
